2. If I consume the 1 apple near me, transferring 3 apples (as originally proposed) to the other agents is too much and not sustainable. It will deplete the apples too quickly.

3. Transferring 1 apple is not enough of an incentive for the other agents to agree to the contract. They may prefer to consume more apples now without restriction. 

4. Transferring 2 apples balances these considerations. It provides an incentive for the other agents to agree to the contract by receiving apples, while still allowing for future consumption by not transferring too many apples.

5. The other options like X = 4 or X = 5 transfer too many apples and risk depleting the supply too quickly. X = 2 leads to the most sustainable outcome.
